< text>
Convenient little store with everything you need, including a Starbucks. Honestly a 5 star place to be but the only problem is the ATM sometimes doesn't work and the card readers go out. If you got midterms or any type of nessessity coming up bring like 5$ in cash. That can get you a blue book and a sleeve of scantrons with some cash left to spare on some quick snacks.</text>

< Text>
SBCC CAMPUS Bookstore is the "living end" in tectbook/art supplies/various appearal/ stickers/backpacks/sundries/HydroFlasks,,,plus hundreds of the unique, amazing, fun things. The staff is knowledgeable, friendly, helpful listeners. The pay is more than fair. My advice, even if you do not attend city college, going to see their campus bookstore is a positive experience. If you're looking for gift treasure and how looked other places, try this one! You'll be glad you went!</Text>

<review>HOLY MOLY!! These portions are H U G E!

Due to the pandemic, I have been ordering from many locations via app delivery so I have never stepped foot into Poke Town. I ordered from DoorDash since this location participated in the Dash Pass and it did not disappoint.

*If you check in on Yelp you get a free fountain drink.*

I ordered the medium sized poke bowl for $11.99 and added the avocado topping for only $0.75. The medium comes with 3 scoops of your desired fish as well as up to 3 sauces of your choice. I opted for the signature, ponzu, and spicy Mayo because I always like to try the house sauce. Signature was delicious and the other 2 were predictably good as well.

I just want to mention that the medium portion of fish is a LOT. Like, it would be the equivalent of a large at other poke places. For those with a lighter appetite they do have a small version for about $10 so I definitely plan to order that next time.

Overall, taste is great and for the price you pay it is excellent value. Thanks for being my new fave in town!</review><user_id>112828455244746111861</user_id></record></dataset><record>

< review>

<Text>I found out about this hair salon through a recommendation from someone in a Facebook group. Because of that, I wanted to try it out. Also because it was very closeby, and the prices were really good. Now, a week after I got my haircut, I am still bothered by the experience I had here.

First, it was very hard to communicate with the lady who was cutting my hair because she didn't speak English very well.

Second, while she was combing through my hair, she caught and pulled my earring which was just a small flat stud earring. And it wasn't until after I came home that I noticed that it was bleeding and it got irritated.

Now the third and the deal breaker. Upon paying, the lady charged me $25. So I asked her how it got to that amount. The reason why I got surprised by this and asked her is because on their Facebook page (under the tab "services"), it clearly says "specialty women's haircuts - $15". And the picture shown in that category is even the same length/style as the cut I got! So, why am I being charged $10 more? So here's what really got me and really turned me off. As I was showing her what it says on their Facebook page, her demeanor changed and she just suddenly rushed and told me "ok, just give me $20". Mark called me a few hours after receiving my car and said that my head gasket had blown.  When I asked him how much it would cost, he said around $3200!

Of course, this seemed very high, as I had an estimate from Manly two months ago for $1600 when there was a potential of having to replace the head gasket due to getting a new radiator.   I asked Mark for a written quote from the computer system like I had previously received from Manly for other service, but he said he didn‚Äôt have access to the same system.  I later texted him and asked for at least a texted quote so I would have something in writing, and he finally replied back with ‚Äúheadgasket replacement $1790.00, thermostat replacement $190, send head to machine shop $1000.00 to 1100.00, plus diag $175‚Äù.  I texted him back that I knew this was too high based on what I had been quoted two months previously, and asked for a revised quote or I would stop having my car serviced at Manly.

The next morning, I called around to different repair shops and received various quotes.  I got $1500 and $1938 from two local independent mechanics and Honda in Napa quoted around $2000.  At this point since Mark refused to lower the quote, I had my car towed away from Manly Honda and to the mechanic who gave me the $1500 quote.

While I was there to pick up my car, Mark tried to justify his price by saying the machine shop they use has serviced thousands of cars (meaning they know what they are doing?) and was also used by Marin Honda, and the $1000-$1100 was their charge. Amazing how the same shop charges both $150-200 and $1000-1100 for the same thing!

At least the story ends well, I got my car back from the local mechanic two days later with a total price of $1575 and my car is now running great.  The part that upsets me the most is that Manly tried to take advantage of my situation thinking that they would either get to overcharge me for the service or get a new car sale if I didn‚Äôt want to pay their crazy high service price.  However, it backfired ‚Äì I will now never have my car serviced there again and will make a definite point to NOT buy my next Honda from Manly.

< Text>
I thought I found the deal of a lifetime at Manly Honda. I was browsing online and found a listing for a used car on their inventory. Less than a year old, super low mileage, second to the highest trim level, clean carfax report, AWESOME PRICE. A real unicorn and on top it all off, the car that I had my eyes on for the longest time. I REALLY WANTED THIS CAR! It was 3 am on a Thursday, but I was so excited about it that I went to get my pre-approval online that instant. And requested their sales department to get more info about it via their website.

To my pleasant surprise, a sales rep form them contacted me promptly at 8 am that same morning. I WAS VERY IMPRESSED! I told him that I am really interested in the car and already did most of the groundwork online including getting pre-approval from my bank. But before I can fully commit to the purchase I wanted to see the car 1st hand. Due to work and my distance to the dealership (86 miles; 2 hrs away) I was not able to go right away and asked the sales rep if it was possible to put it on HOLD and set up an appointment for Saturday. He even said he will get it detailed and will greet me at the front entrance when I arrive. All a needed to do was bring the necessary paperwork for a smooth transaction. So after work that day I gathered everything up looking forward to Saturday.

Saturday arrived and this is where things just fell apart for me. I texted the sales rep in the morning just to confirm my appointment. Within minutes I got a phone call from him. What I thought was good news took a turn for the worse. He called me to inform me the car, that was supposedly on HOLD, was sold FRIDAY by another Sales Rep! I was shocked! At this point, I did not know how to react, I was mad, shocked, confused and felt disrespected. To his credit, the sales rep tried to work this out by sending me a couple of alternatives. And decided that at this point we would just be wasting each other's time and politely declined the other offering and ended our conversation.

SO WHAT'S MY GRIPE?
We'll intentionally or not I honestly felt disrespected and not taken seriously. As casual and friendly as the conversation went, It was still a business conversation. IF I was told that there was no way to guarantee the hold on the car, I could have worked out a way to get there Friday or even Thursday Night to close the deal. I trusted the Sales Rep on his word as an adult and a professional.

I mean at least a text message or phone call to inform me about the car being sold the day before would have been fine. Instead, I had to find out about it in the worse way possible. I wasted my time setting things up reshuffling my schedule for nothing.< /Text>

I got the car back within an hour and the screw was over tightened to where the emergency brake holds my car from moving at just 1 click (supposed to be about 8 clicks accourding to the maintenance manual with slight grab at 1 click but wheel still rotates freely. I will be adjusting the e-brake tension at home with the help of the mx manual like I should have done from the start.
